Economic Special

Responsibilities of the National Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau 167

— Bao Yi

Recently, the Ministry of Finance, in accordance with the decision of the Executive Yuan, established the National Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau to take overall control of grain purchasing, transportation, sales, and surplus/deficit regulation. This Transportation and Sales Bureau was once proposed in the 23rd year (of the Republic, i.e., 1934), but failed to materialize due to various constraints. However, the Transportation and Sales Bureau has always been of great significance in solving the overall grain problem. Now that the matter has been brought up again and the Transportation and Sales Bureau is being actively prepared, it is necessary to study its proper tasks and considerations.

It is generally believed that the crux of China's grain problem is the reduction in per-unit arable land productivity combined with frequent disasters, rather than an absolute factor of grain panic. In years of poor harvest, landlords and grain merchants hoarding and speculating often cause grain prices to rise beyond the limits of natural increases, which illustrates that the defects of social and economic organization can surpass natural causes and lead to grain panic. The Transportation and Sales Bureau, in handling the regulation of grain surpluses and deficits, must recognize that the uneven distribution of grain is a problem even more significant than the issue of total output.

At the same time, because of the simplicity of domestic transportation and the complexity of transaction procedures, even if the harvests vary from region to region, and theoretically can be adjusted, in reality, it is still necessary to rely on foreign grain. In disaster years, when grain prices are high, foreign grain pours in, which helps to suppress prices; however, in the same season, the harvest regions still suffer from the phenomenon of low grain prices hurting farmers. In a good harvest year, grain prices should fall, but often fall beyond the natural decline due to the import or dumping of foreign grain (Note 1); sometimes they are too expensive due to foreign purchases (Note 2). The impact of the international market on China's grain surpluses and deficits does not meet the actual needs of China's national conditions. The fundamental reason, of course, is the fluctuation of grain prices. When foreign grain prices fall or Chinese grain prices rise, foreign grain imports increase; when foreign grain prices rise or Chinese grain prices fall, foreign grain imports decrease. The amount of foreign grain imports shifts with the level of domestic grain prices; on the other hand, domestic grain prices are not simply determined by the amount of production. Therefore, the anarchic state of foreign grain imports leads to an increasingly chaotic domestic grain market. The interrelationship between domestic and foreign grain prices is the second key point to be noted by the Transportation and Sales Bureau.

The tasks of the Transportation and Sales Bureau include the operation of purchasing, stockpiling, transporting, and selling. The main key, however, is the control of grain prices. This is because the fluctuation of grain prices can affect the quantity and regional distribution of purchasing, stockpiling, transporting, and selling. In terms of the transportation and sales of inland grain, the amount of grain that grain merchants collect from various towns is determined by the profit remaining after deducting transportation costs and intermediary fees from the inland grain price when converted to the urban grain price. When the converted amount of the two grain prices cannot maintain the profit of the grain merchants, the grain merchants will abandon the domestic grain and compete to purchase foreign grain (Note 3). In terms of the monopoly of landlords and grain merchants, most of the grain is transferred from poor farmers to the stockpiles of landlords and grain merchants, and the profit rate given to landlords and grain merchants by short-term and long-term grain prices becomes the standard for stockpiling or selling. If the elasticity of price fluctuations can be reduced, the possibility of landlords and grain merchants speculating for profit will naturally be reduced, and the circulation of grain can maintain a normal state. Then, the determination of the highest and lowest grain prices becomes the theme of transportation and sales.

Controlling grain prices starts with determining the highest and lowest grain prices, and at the same time, it is necessary to organically use all the processes involved in transportation and sales. For example, when grain prices fall in a bumper year, the Transportation and Sales Bureau stipulates a minimum price based on domestic and foreign grain price indices, price indices, and production costs, and purchases at a high price, or exports through state-owned enterprises (Note 4). The purchased grain is stored on the one hand, and continuously transported to various consumption areas on the other hand, either for sale or for continued storage in preparation for price stabilization in the coming year. If there is a shortage in a year of poor harvest and prices soar, the Transportation and Sales Bureau will still set a maximum price with reference to domestic and foreign grain price indices and price indices, so that landlords and grain merchants know that grain prices will not rise further and will sell their grain one after another. On the one hand, the grain stored over the years is sold at a reduced price, and on the other hand, the import tax on foreign grain is waived. When necessary, purchases are made from China and abroad, or resold, or used to replenish storage. The purchase of foreign grain at high prices must be approved by the Transportation and Sales Bureau in its overall plan. In short, according to the grain price control policy, all transportation and sales matters must be organized and promoted. Therefore, the Transportation and Sales Bureau needs affiliated agencies that are interconnected and coordinated.

According to the organization of the Japanese Rice Bureau, it is divided into rice policy, survey of inland areas, foreign areas, management, and other sections, as well as rice offices. The Rice Policy Section is responsible for various surveys on rice policy, surveys on the exchange of rice supply and demand, rice storage incentives, affairs of rice offices and their offices, and affairs not under the jurisdiction of other sections. The Survey Section is responsible for surveys on rice production costs, surveys on the existing amount of rice, surveys on rice movement, standard minimum and maximum prices, rice processing, transportation, storage, exchange, lending, exchange, processing, and arrangement, the scope of rice with officially set minimum and maximum prices and their price differences, and reporting on certain articles of the Rice Control Enforcement Ordinance. The Foreign Section is responsible for the purchase, sale, storage, exchange, processing, and arrangement of rice from Korea, Taiwan, or foreign countries, all permissions for rice import and export, restrictions on the import of millet, sorghum, and glutinous millet, and increases, decreases, or exemptions of import taxes on rice, millet, sorghum, and glutinous millet. The Foreign Rice Affairs Survey Section is responsible for the adjustment of the special account for rice supply and demand, state-owned property, articles, and construction belonging to the aforementioned account, and the sorting and summarizing of rice-related parts of general accounting matters. The Rice Office is responsible for matters related to the Rice Law (Note 5). The spirit of the Chinese Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau can be said to be completely the same as that of the Japanese Rice Bureau. Therefore, the internal organization of the Transportation and Sales Bureau should at least include rice policy surveys, inland, foreign, management, and other sections, as well as rice offices. The relationship between the sections forms the foundation of the Transportation and Sales Bureau's function, and each section proceeds in a coordinated manner in a comprehensive policy. However, due to financial difficulties, the affiliated agencies of each section cannot be widely distributed and deeply rooted in the countryside. The Transportation and Sales Bureau can appoint commissioners to work jointly with the county governments of various counties. Everything is directly commanded by the competent authorities of the Transportation and Sales Bureau and follows an independent special accounting system, and the funds of the Transportation and Sales Bureau are never mixed with the expenses of the county governments. The existing installations related to grain and general industrial and commercial economic construction, such as the Ministries of Interior, Finance, Communications, Railways, and special agencies, must cooperate according to the requirements of the Transportation and Sales Bureau.

However, the Transportation and Sales Bureau must also pay attention to two points: first, in grain price control, the function of stipulating the maximum price is greater than the function of stipulating the minimum price; second, the existing agricultural warehouses and local granaries should all be operated by the Transportation and Sales Bureau. Regarding the first point, due to the prevalence of rent in kind and grain loans, many farmers pay land rent or repay debts with their harvest, and few sell it voluntarily. The ownership of grain in the market mostly belongs to landlords and grain merchants. Stipulating a minimum price and purchasing at a high price is beneficial to landlords and grain merchants but not to poor farmers. Furthermore, the purchasing policy causes poor farmers to purchase food at high prices during the period of shortage (Note 6). This problem is related to the entire production system, and the Transportation and Sales Bureau cannot cope with it. However, precisely because landlords and grain merchants manipulate grain production, the unlimited increase in grain prices is most harmful to general consumers and poor farmers. Therefore, stipulating a maximum price and suppressing grain prices mainly harms landlords and grain merchants. The significance of protecting consumers and poor farmers is actually deeper than the effect of the minimum price. When the Transportation and Sales Bureau uses the grain price control strategy, this point should be clearly distinguished. Regarding the second point, the Transportation and Sales Bureau should establish a systematic and unified storage agency. Storage is an important stage in the transportation and sales process and functions as a regulator. Although existing farmers' warehouses have the form of storage, the grain stored in them is mostly owned by wealthy farmers, landlords, and grain merchants. Therefore, not only can they not regulate grain prices, but they can disrupt grain prices. Moreover, the financial assistance function of agricultural warehouses is of no benefit to most farming families who have no grain to mortgage. Therefore, the Transportation and Sales Bureau can borrow circulating funds from the financial sector to reorganize the national agricultural warehouses, simplify the function of agricultural warehouses, and turn them into specialized storage places in the grain control policy. The circulation of agricultural finance is then the responsibility of the Agricultural Bank. As for other local storage, the main purpose is to prepare for famine and relieve poverty. The ability of local granaries to stabilize grain prices is often offset by the influence of grain from other regions. Only when the national grain price control policy is implemented and local granaries follow the planned instructions of the Transportation and Sales Bureau can it be effective. Farmers' warehouses and local granaries are all under the control of the Transportation and Sales Bureau, and all stored grain can be transported to various places in advance (Note 7) or temporarily as needed. In short, it must correspond to the stability of grain prices and the regulation of surpluses and deficits.

The National Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau bears a major mission for the solution of China's entire grain problem. Its main task should be the control of grain prices. Whether it is purchasing, stockpiling, transporting, or selling, it must be carried out organically under the control of grain prices in order to exert the full function of transportation and sales; at the same time, attention must be paid to the special roles of wealthy farmers, landlords, and grain merchants, as well as foreign grain, in the domestic grain market.

(Note 1) In the year of the great flood in 1931 and the bumper harvest in 1932, the import of foreign rice was either very little or, on the contrary, more. The reason is that in the bumper year of 1930, 1931 was sufficient for self-sufficiency (referring to the Yangtze River basin). By the time of the great flood, it was already early autumn. At that time, what caused panic was the people's food for the coming year. Merchants ordered foreign rice, so although there was a bumper harvest, the import of foreign rice was more, and the rice price fell beyond the appropriate limit.

(Note 2) This year there was a bumper harvest in almost the entire country, but some people took the opportunity to come to China to purchase, and the grain price unexpectedly rose, which is a phenomenon that should not occur in a bumper year.

(Note 3) "Improving Rice and Wheat and Equalizing Transportation" by Cao Yumin, Nationalities Magazine, Volume 3, Issue 12, page 2036:

(Note 4) Article 2 of the Interim Measures for Food Regulation promulgated by the Executive Yuan this year allows exports. The basis is that the food market price this year is not significantly different from the same period last year, and according to customs reports, food imports in the first ten months of this year were far above exports. However, wheat prices have risen in various countries this year, and Japan has also purchased large quantities of rice from China, Siam, and Annam. The export of rice and grain from Siam and Annam to China is also decreasing. If China allows exports without restrictions, there will be no supplementary measures for grain next year. It is necessary for the Transportation and Sales Bureau to handle the so-called state-owned exports.

(Note 5) "Rural Cooperation and Agricultural Warehouses in Japan" by Xu Yuanruo, page 11:

(Note 6) Stipulating a minimum price and purchasing grain at a high price only benefits wealthy farmers, landlords, and grain merchants, while poor farmers receive no benefit. This is the predicament encountered by the Japanese Wealthy Farmers Grain Control Law.

(Note 7) This year, there was a bumper harvest, but the Yuehan Railway could not transport it in time, resulting in a trend of importing foreign rice in Guangdong Province. If the Transportation and Sales Bureau makes an overall plan, after the harvest season, the surplus grain from the producing areas of Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui can be gradually transported to Guangdong for storage and regulation in the coming year. The grain in the producing areas will be purchased by the Transportation and Sales Bureau, and the grain price will not fall due to the temporary congestion of production. Every year, it is announced that the surplus grain from the producing areas will be gradually transported to the sales areas, and the price will not be expensive due to the lack of transportation. The Transportation and Sales Bureau must manage the transportation and sales in the form of purchasing and storage. This is also one of the reasons.

A Review of Grain Control in Various Provinces (Continued) 168

— Li Yinbei

Anhui: Anhui Province is also a rice-surplus province; the various ports in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River and rice-deficient coastal provinces often rely on the supply of rice from Wuhu. Therefore, the rice production in Anhui Province is also very important in the food status of our country. This year, the Anhui provincial authorities are dealing with the province's food problem: first, they are taking the warehousing policy as the center, and the source of its storage mortgage funds is provided by the Shanghai China Agricultural Credit Syndicate; the person in charge of the syndicate has signed an agricultural warehouse credit contract of one million yuan with the Construction and Finance Departments, and the Provincial Agricultural Warehouse Management Office is designated to build provincial warehouses in twenty-four counties including Fengyang; county warehouses are generally set up in other counties; the provincial and county warehouses will be completed before the end of September. The heads of each warehouse have also received agricultural loan business from the syndicate office in accordance with regulations. Subsequently, the issue of grain being exported abroad arose, and people from North China went to Anhui to absorb a large amount of rice, and good merchants went deep into the countryside to search for rice from farmers to be transported to the north. This resulted in scarce sources on the market and soaring grain prices. At this point, the authorities decided to issue an order banning the export of Anhui rice to remedy the situation. However, neighboring provinces and cities can still be assisted with the approval of formal civilian applications. As a result, the grain trade in Anhui Province is managed by the provincial government. As for the future storage and transportation of rice in the province, the Construction Department is drafting a plan for selling Anhui rice to Guangdong.

B. Rice Self-Sufficient Provinces

Jiangsu: Jiangsu is the province with the most fluid rice and grain. The rice imported over the years is not for consumption in the province; and the rice exported is not all produced in the province. It is estimated that Jiangsu's grain production is sufficient in normal years. Since the problem of national rice leaking to the sea, it has been severely felt. The provincial government, fearing the years of shortage and that traitors would transport grain to support the enemy, passed ten articles of the "Temporary Measures for Strictly Prohibiting the Export of Food in Jiangsu Province" at a provincial government meeting on October 27; ordering all subordinate regions to strictly prohibit the export of food. Thereupon, the province's food trade was under the strict supervision of the provincial authorities. (Note: It has been decided to abolish it at the provincial government meeting on December 8)

C. Rice Deficient Provinces

Zhejiang: Generally speaking, Zhejiang Province feels that there is a food shortage every year; specifically, surpluses and deficits are actually mutually visible. For example, Ningbo and Shaoxing need the assistance of foreign rice, while Wenzhou and Taizhou have a large outflow every year. Therefore, it can be proved that Zhejiang is a rice-deficient province. The Zhejiang provincial authorities' policy for dealing with this year's food problem is centered on warehousing: the aim is to achieve the goal of "Zhejiang people eating Zhejiang rice." Therefore, the province's agricultural warehouse business is divided into three categories: (1) Provincial agricultural warehouses, (2) County agricultural warehouses, (3) Township warehouses. The construction of provincial agricultural warehouses is funded by the provincial authorities borrowing 400,000 yuan in agricultural warehouse construction loans from the Farmers Bank of China; four provincial warehouses are designated to be built in Jinhua, AoJiang, Haimen, and Xiashi. The loan term is three years, with a weekly interest rate of one percent. Only interest is paid this year, and repayment of principal begins in the twenty-sixth year. Now the loan contract has been approved by the Provincial Payment Conference, and both parties can officially sign it. In terms of county agricultural warehouses, it has been decided to borrow and renovate the original county granaries, and no new warehouses will be built to save expenses. In terms of township warehouses, it is stipulated that the original township warehouses will be temporarily borrowed for use. The number of county, township, and town warehouses in each county is stipulated to be at least one. In addition to the provincial agricultural warehouses, which are stipulated to be completed before the autumn harvest next year, county, township, and town warehouses are all limited to being prepared by the end of September this year for storage and mortgage this autumn. The source of funds for storage and mortgage is also provided by the Farmers Bank of China, and the total amount is said to be 3 million yuan; however, it can be increased at any time depending on the actual needs. However, since the issue of national rice leaking to the sea arose, the authorities drafted nine articles of the "Outline of Measures for Food Adjustment in Zhejiang Province" by the Department of Civil Affairs in order to prevent it from affecting the people's food in Zhejiang Province. It was submitted to the 866th Provincial Government Conference for approval, and the Department of Civil Affairs ordered it to be followed. As a result, the rice destined for various places in Zhejiang was detained in Changdi; the entire food trade in Zhejiang Province was shrouded in the control of the provincial government.

Henan: Henan is also a grain-deficient province. Before the issue of national rice being exported abroad had just sprouted, the Henan provincial authorities, in view of the concern that a large amount of summer-harvested wheat and grain would leak to the sea; therefore, the provincial government passed six articles of the "Temporary Measures for Grain Export from Henan Province" for control. Therefore, this year's grain trade in Henan Province was the first to be managed by the provincial authorities this autumn.

Shandong: Shandong Province has an annual excess of imports of grain; its shortage is self-evident. Since the beginning of autumn this year, the crops in various counties have had a bumper harvest. The people of Shandong are celebrating; but the problem of national rice being exported abroad is becoming increasingly serious. The provincial government has repeatedly received telegrams from coastal counties in Jiaodong; a certain country is instigating unscrupulous merchants to purchase grain for export; and since northern Shandong borders Hebei, it is really unimaginable if strict prohibitions are not imposed! Therefore, on October 20, it was proposed to the Provincial Government Conference to study the measures. As a result, it was decided to hand it over to the Civil Affairs, Finance, and Construction Departments to jointly plan the grain ban policy. Recently, the Provincial Standing Committee has also strictly prohibited the export of grain.

In addition, there are still some provinces; such as Shanxi Province, which, on November 4, instructed the Datong-Puzhou Railway Bureau to prepare vehicles to transport the grain stored in southern Tianjin to Taiyuan. Either because food control has not yet been implemented, or because the region is special, food control cannot be implemented; the former includes provinces such as Fujian and Guangdong, and the latter includes the Hebei-Chahar authorities, which will be discussed separately.

(3) Advantages and Disadvantages of Grain Control Measures

Let us try to look at the provinces that have already implemented food control. Generally speaking, in rice-surplus provinces, the focus is on improving transportation and sales through warehousing policies; in rice-deficient provinces, the focus is on warehousing policies and supervising grain trade. Now, let us discuss their advantages and disadvantages separately. First, let's talk about its advantages:

(1) Prompt Handling: China's food administration has obviously entered a state of discussing without deciding and deciding without acting. For example, the food problem has had a consensus on unified control of transportation and sales for several years; however, it has been entangled in various ways, and the case has not been resolved so far. The new grain has been on the market this time, and grain prices have soared. Although there are many reasons for this; the most terrible thing is that traitors are transporting grain to support the enemy! This kind of problem cannot be compared with ordinary food problems. If emergency measures are not taken to block it; and if it is handled in accordance with the administrative procedures of reporting to the county, the county reporting to the province, and the province reporting to the central government for instructions. It will inevitably delay the people's food supply. It must be known that unscrupulous merchants transporting grain to leak to the sea is a non-public secret operation; the agility of their work can be described as miraculous, making it really difficult to monitor. If it is not resolved quickly on the spot, a large amount of food can be completely lost in an instant! This time, the provinces have adopted this emergency measure to ban grain exports, which is one of the emergency measures.

(2) Local Problems Solved by Local Authorities: The entire food problem in China can be divided into three: (1) Production cannot be self-sufficient, (2) The warehousing system is not prepared, (3) Transportation and sales methods are not good. However, strictly speaking: under the premise of these three food problems, its nature can still be distinguished into two categories: (1) Food problems with national consistency, (2) Local food problems. The former should be solved by the central government's overall planning; the latter must be solved by the local authorities adapting to local conditions. As far as the warehousing and sales policies of various provinces this year are concerned: they are quite worthy of praise. For example, Anhui and Jiangxi provinces are both rice-surplus areas, while Zhejiang is a rice-deficient province; in terms of their local food problems: if the former allows the surplus rice production to flood the market, the rice farmers in the province will inevitably suffer widespread losses due to cheap grain hurting farmers; the latter allows farmers to sell all the rice they have, and they will inevitably suffer the danger of spring famine next year. Therefore, the only solution is to promote the warehousing policy to regulate it. Next, take Hunan as an example: Hunan rice has always been a surplus area; its local food problem is the same as that of Anhui and Jiangxi provinces. Now, Hunan Province is improving transportation and sales as a starting point, and selling Hunan rice to Guangdong; its function is also the same as the warehousing policy. For most of the food problems containing locality, it is best to be solved by the local government that is down-to-earth. Solving the local problems that are closely related to the local government has about four benefits: (1) Cost savings, (2) A sense of responsibility, (3) Recognizing the core of the problem, (4) Easy to manage.

The above is the advantage of the food control in various provinces this time; the following will discuss the shortcomings.

(1) Provinces Govern Themselves: Lack of Contact: The biggest drawback of this food control in various provinces is that they only know that the provinces govern themselves and do not know how to contact each other for overall planning. It is obviously very different from the "national unified division of labor and cooperation" method previously advocated by the author. For example, in terms of the sales policy of Hunan, Anhui, and Jiangxi provinces: since the news of Hunan rice being sold to Guangdong has spread, the rice production in Anhui and Jiangxi provinces has mistakenly believed that Guangdong Province is a huge rice warehouse; therefore, they all plan to sell the surplus rice to Guangdong Province to see if it can accommodate the rice from the three provinces. In fact, it is predicted that it will inevitably fail. It must be known that although Guangdong is a rice-deficient province, it is closely connected with rice-producing areas such as Annam and Siam, which are known as the "Granary of the South." According to the customs reports over the years: the import of foreign rice in Guangdong Province accounts for an average of about two-thirds of the total import of foreign rice in the country every year. It can be seen that the people's food in Guangdong Province is still insufficient, but it is not difficult to rely on foreign rice to make up for it. And this time, Hunan rice being sold to Guangdong is no different from taking the market of foreign rice and replacing it. Just imagine whether the countries that produce foreign rice will give up if the original foreign rice market is occupied? If we speculate based on the current situation, there are many hidden reefs in the future! Since the news of Hunan rice being sold to Guangdong spread, the price of rice in Changsha has been rising day by day; the provincial government, fearing that it would affect the cost of Hunan rice being sold to Guangdong, instructed the counties and cities on October 25 to announce to merchants: to support the plan of Hunan rice being sold to Guangdong, and not to take the opportunity to manipulate and violate the sales contract. From this, it can be seen that those who are plotting from it obviously have other intentions; trying to hinder the active progress of Hunan rice being sold to Guangdong. The Shantou Grain Industry Association has held meetings many times and publicly opposed it. On the surface, it is an expression of a small number of people who want to manipulate the rice market; but in fact, they have sent people to Hong Kong to contact the North and South Banks to seek solutions. And the North and South Banks have heard that they sympathize with this move; they plan to increase their capital and set up foreign rice transportation and sales offices in Guangzhou and Shantou. And the Huoxi Grain Industry in Saigon and Yangon is also willing to provide backing and support. The Huoxi Grain Industry has a close relationship with the North and South Banks in Hong Kong; the sale of foreign rice to Guangdong over the years has been handled by the North and South Banks on special ships. Now that they are colluding in this way, we really cannot ignore it. It is expected that when Hunan rice enters Guangdong, the price of foreign rice will inevitably fall and be dumped. What's more, the movement to request the reduction and exemption of foreign rice import tax in Guangdong Province continues, this is the second. And according to the latest news from the Roman Telegraph: According to the report published by the International Institute of Agriculture, the area of rice planting in the entire territory of India, including Qingdian, this year is estimated to be about 31,748,000 hectares. According to last year, it increased by 2.8%. (See Shen Bao, November 2) India and Qingdian are also the source of foreign rice supply for our country. With the increase in their production, their surplus grain will inevitably be dumped in China. Guangdong Province is a close neighbor of foreign rice dumping, and of course it will not be abandoned by Indian and Qingdian grain. This is the third. However, let us try to think about the biggest purpose of Hunan rice being sold to Guangdong: to seek the adjustment of Hunan's surplus rice production through transportation and sales, so as not to threaten the tragic decline of Hunan rice prices; so that all Hunan rice farmers can avoid the attack of bumper harvests turning into disasters. Now, due to these various reasons, the result will inevitably outweigh the gains. If we allow Anhui rice and Jiangxi rice to be sold to Guangdong without a plan, it will only help foreign rice to dump and disrupt the market; it will inevitably create a situation where Guangdong has rice but no market. Therefore, this move is good in itself; but before the event, the provinces govern themselves and only know how to blindly promote it, without the overall planning between provinces, I am afraid that the future results will not be optimistic.

(2) Banning Grain Exports is Not Something that Provinces Can Handle: Although the policies of the provinces that are currently implementing grain bans are different, a common point can be found in their implementation of grain ban measures. That is, the provinces that implement grain bans generally focus on banning grain "exports" and focus on supervising "exit from the province." In fact, banning grain from leaking to the sea is a food problem of national consistency, which is definitely not something that a local province can handle. For example, if Province A is implementing a grain ban, while Province B is still freely circulating; those who are slippery will take advantage of the shortcomings of our country's lack of coordination, and transport and leak it repeatedly, then the result will be that those who ban it will ban it themselves, and those who leak it will leak it themselves. This is the first. Although the coastal ports in our country can be strictly blocked: the barriers along the Great Wall in North China have long been lost. If the central government implements a grain ban policy, and the domestic circulation of grain is still not prohibited; but the inflow of grain into North China is different from leaking to the sea for export. From this, we can know that banning grain exports feels very tricky everywhere, this is the second. Under the combination of these two impossible grain bans, the legitimate grain prices in various provinces will inevitably be heavily hindered by the transformation of taxes due to the grain ban. The legitimate rice farmers will make grain as cheap as mud due to rumors spread by traitors. Mutually激盪, the people's food problem of the general public will become more serious due to the implementation of the grain ban.

(3) No Permanence: The final point of the current food control in various provinces is the lack of durability. It must be known that the food problem in our country has been around for a long time; it is definitely not something that can be solved by the temporary response of the provinces recently.

(4) Conclusion

For the sake of today's plan. In addition to continuing to work hard according to the late Premier's instruction to operate the food purpose "not to redeem money, but to provide for the people"; the author can contribute two food routes in the future at this time, to be used for reference.

(1) The recent implementation of food control in various provinces; its advantages are indeed facts; but its shortcomings cannot be denied by us. If we can improve its shortcomings and utilize its advantages, it will be of some help to the future of the people's food. Therefore, the author advocates the first food route, that is, for the provinces that have recently implemented food control, the various facilities related to the grain trade should be reorganized into grain transportation and sales offices to manage the matter. On the one hand, local food control is used to assist the Central Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau in its work; at the same time, it relies on the consistent food policy of the central government to eliminate the spirit of provincial self-government and lack of coordination.

(2) The indecision of our country's food control is actually due to too much emphasis on the control of the grain trade. The entire food economy includes three categories: production, transportation and sales, and consumption; the current food production is only focused on controlling transportation and sales. However, the control of grain transportation and sales is more difficult to implement; it must be known that those who are currently standing on the side of rice producers are not the majority of food consumers; but a part of the grain financiers and grain dealers. Food control is abandoned after the control of grain production and the consumption of the consumer as a shield, and lonely control of transportation and sales; therefore, its anti-resistance is only seen. Therefore, the author advocates the second food line, that is, the future food control should not be resolved by controlling transportation and sales as a way to solve the problem; but by controlling the production and consumption of food as a starting point. Once the production and consumption of food have a clue, the control of transportation and sales will not be difficult to solve, otherwise, I am afraid that it will be a waste of effort. How can the two words "manage" and "handle" solve the transportation and sales of food? (End)

### Finance: Money Exchange Industry Advises Yin Copper Coins to Depreciate 169

Because more than a month ago, Hongkou's small money houses purchased silver, copper coins and small foreign exchange in the dark market, and some were transported to other ports, resulting in the exchange rate suddenly falling below the determined exchange rate. Notice: According to the instructions of the Social Affairs Bureau, the recent sudden drop in copper coins and small foreign exchange below the legal exchange rate, the Bureau has instructed the Association to find ways to stop it, etc. Upon receipt of this, from now on, all transactions must be carried out in accordance with the legal price, and no increase or decrease is allowed. This is hereby notified, and all are requested to pay attention.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 175

— (Xiao Bai)

Life is full of sorrow and hardship, yet it is also sweet and bright.

In the course of a person's life history, its development is often not linear, but proceeds in curves. It will inevitably encounter many obstacles and dangers along the way. However, it is precisely perseverance and struggle that break through these heavy obstacles!

It is said that the survival of mankind is always governed by "hope." No matter what kind of person in the world, there is no one who does not hold hope. Indeed, the hopes of some of these people are reasonable, while others harbor extravagant hopes, daydreams, or even absurd fantasies. However, they all rely on their own hope as the basis for survival. It is the same. "Hope is truly the mother of the evolution of human society!

History has determined our fate and placed us in an extremely distressing and turbulent era. To overcome this distress and resolve this turmoil, we not only need courage and sacrifice, but also a clear understanding of the goals of our struggle, a glorious and clear self-confidence, coupled with arduous and unremitting struggle!

Huaqing Pool 176

— Yang Gong Huai

Huaqing Pool. It was where Chairman Chiang Kai-shek stayed the night before he was kidnapped to Xi'an, located south of Lintong County, on Mount Li. There are hot springs on the mountain. Emperor Taizong of the Tang Dynasty built the Tangquan Palace here, and Emperor Xuanzong changed it to Huaqing Palace, further developing the hot spring wells into pools. Yang Guifei (Imperial Concubine Yang) once bathed here, hence Bai Juyi's "Song of Everlasting Regret" contains the line, "In early spring, she was bestowed a bath at Huaqing Pool, where the warm spring waters were smooth and washed away her creamy skin." In front of the pool, there is a wooden archway with the three characters "Huaqing Pool" inscribed on it, written by Yu Youren, the President of the Control Yuan. Passing through the archway, weeping willows line the path, creating a serene and secluded landscape. The pool is located within Huaqing Park and is managed by the China Travel Service, using the profits to develop Huaqing Pool. The current facilities of the pool are mostly Europeanized. The pool is divided into two: one is a single-person pool, and the other is the Guifei (Imperial Concubine) Pool, both paved with small tiles. The Guifei Pool is larger and can accommodate four people bathing together. It is said that the bathing price is one yuan per person. The single-person pool is slightly smaller, but the facilities and bathing price are the same. The water temperature is suitable, with no sulfur odor, so it is most suitable for bathing. Is this why Huaqing Pool enjoys such a great reputation?

Tofu and Celebrities 177

— Xian Yuan

When Mr. Li Shizeng, a member of the Central Committee, studied in Paris in his early years, he specialized in chemistry. One day, he suddenly thought of tofu, the most nourishing food in China, which had never existed in European countries. He specially wrote a treatise expounding the functions of tofu and published it in the Paris Daily. At the same time, he opened a tofu company in Paris, which caused a sensation among people of all kinds in that area. Everyone wanted to taste it quickly. Therefore, the business of Li's tofu company prospered from this. So, tofu going abroad started with Li. Those who talk about the history of tofu must know this.

It is also heard that Wang Tieshan and tofu, Mr. Feng Yuxiang once published an article "Mr. Wang Tieshan, the First-Class Honest Official of Modern Times" in Yijing, which contains the following passage: We have been together this time for almost a year, and we are simply inseparable at all times. What I admire most is that although he has lived in the officialdom all his life, he has not had the slightest bureaucratic habit. He has several good hobbies, one is that he likes to eat tofu. He often squats on the ground to eat it, and it seems very tasty. People living in the world can have a bowl of tofu to eat, and there is no more happiness. I said to him; In the past, Tang Wenzheng Qian'an of the Qing Dynasty was an official to the rank of governor and governor, and the only dish he ate every day was a plate of tofu, so everyone called him tofu soup. You old man can really be regarded as a confidant of him.

October 25, feeling after waking up, suddenly remembering that yesterday was the day after the Double Ninth Festival of the Xia calendar, which was the day of Mao Yi's death eighteen years ago. Danfeng Huangye Zhongren

Glass Cup 178

— Rong Yu

"Glass Cup" is a very popular slang term in Shanghai, known to almost everyone. According to the Six Writings, this is a "semantic association." Because the female tea servants who engage in this occupation do not use teapots or teacups, but glass cups. "By extension of the object to the person," they have the moniker "Glass Cup."

The origin of "Glass Cup" can be traced back to the Immortal World ten years ago. - Located at the corner of Fuzhou Road and Zhejiang Road, it has been closed for many years. - At that time, because the style was novel and quite stimulating, it caused a sensation throughout Shanghai and captivated many frivolous youths. At that time, tourists with "Drunken Old Man" intentions would throw out a one-yuan tip for a cup of tea, still considered skinflint customers in their eyes. Tipping ten or five yuan for a cup of tea, joking around, hoping to achieve special purposes, was not a big deal. Because of the abundant income, it was not easy to seek this occupation at that time. In addition to being beautiful and young, they also had to have a special means of winning over tourists.

Subsequently, various entertainment venues followed suit, and female tea servants poured in like "carp crossing the river," with all kinds of appearances, ages, and colors. Their careers were not as good as before. For the sake of the environment and life, some of them had no choice but to engage in special transactions. This is not a slander by the author. At least six or seven out of ten are engaged in this transaction. If you don't believe it, look at the pink cases and rape and murder incidents in the newspapers. Female tea servants account for a considerable number.

Speaking of their lives, it's also quite pitiful. Their tea-making places are always contracted by a boss. In addition to providing a meager dinner, the boss has to pay a tea fee of two cents for each cup of tea brewed. The remaining income is enjoyed under his name. If there are few tea-making guests, or they only eat soup dumplings, then they will also be subjected to the boss's cold sarcasm. Therefore, female tea servants with slightly poorer appearances and less skillful flirting methods often complain about their miserable lives, shouting that it is difficult to eat.

The Pears of Zunhua 179

— Zhu Yiren

Every year when it comes time to eat "pears," I always think of the "Buddha's Delight" pear that I ate in Zunhua County, Hebei Province.

"Buddha's Delight" is a special product of Zunhua. When it is sold everywhere, it is collectively called "Tianjin Pear." In fact, there are not so many real "Buddha's Delight" pears. At the same time, it is indeed more delicious than other pears.

"Buddha's Delight" is a sweet, crisp, tender, and delicate Ya pear. Especially the kind of pear that is eaten on the spot in Zunhua, from the time it is picked from the tree to the stalls for sale, the time elapsed is at most one day. Its freshness is really unmatched by other pears. This point is that those who have not personally visited Zunhua do not enjoy the right to eat fresh "Buddha's Delight."

The meaning of the sign "Four Seasons Fresh Fruits" at Shuiye shop is to prove that fruits are most delicious when they are fresh. Therefore, Zunhua's "Buddha's Delight" loses its color once it is transported out of the country. Therefore, you can hardly hear the name "Buddha's Delight" in other places.

When the author was in Zunhua, whenever I was free, I planned to buy pears to eat. My clumsy skill of cutting pears was very pure. Every time I cut off a thin layer of cooked skin, before I even put down the knife in my right hand, I couldn't help but send the jade-like pear in my left hand to my mouth. A mouthful of nectar and jade dew poured into my heart. It really made people anesthetized and unwilling to stop. At the same time, cutting and eating like this was also an economical pastime. Because "Buddha's Delight" only sells for two or three copper coins each locally, it is cheap and good, which is truly worthy of its name.

In one spring, I stayed in a small town "Tiechang Town" more than sixty miles east of Zunhua City for more than a month. When I was free, I would take a walk in the suburbs. When I saw a garden, I would go in and take a look. There were large kinds of pear trees planted there, which were blossoming with snow-white flowers. There were also vines spreading with grape vines. I put myself in this forest of white flowers and green leaves, and I lingered and didn't want to come out. The owner of the garden also said to me with a look of encouragement: "Please come and play in the autumn and eat 'Buddha's Delight'." It's a pity that I couldn't even wait for a summer before I left Tiechang Town, and even said goodbye to the entire Zunhua. Recalling the past, I can't help but feel lost!

Therefore, whenever pears are sold on the market, I am reminded of the scene of eating pears at that time.

I think of "Buddha's Delight", I miss Zunhua where "Buddha's Delight" is produced.

People of Suiyuan 180

— Li Wei

A Er is a waiter in the office. He is from ××, Suiyuan. He is tall, has dark skin, and is quite strong. He usually wears a blue jacket, which seems so old that you can't tell its original color. A line of grease often shines on the collar and cuffs. This is not because he doesn't like cleanliness, but because his economy forces him to do so! Our colleagues treat him very well; he is not only careful in his work, but also able to endure hardship; sometimes when we want something, he knows what it is without us telling him.

However, ever since the war in Suiyuan broke out, his movements have become dull and slow, and under his constantly furrowed eyebrows, his two large, black eyes often emit a fierce light. We knew that he was terrified of the destruction of his hometown and sympathetically forgave him, but the pain he now felt was that he was illiterate and could not read the newspaper to know the outcome of the war.

Every morning, he brought the newspaper in, as if all his strength was used in his hands. He watched us silently reading the newspaper, not knowing what today's news was? He was just anxious beside him, sometimes he couldn't bear it, so he walked gently to my side, his voice trembling slightly, and asked me softly:

"Li Xiansheng, have we won another battle?"

About a few days ago one morning, I told him that on the morning of the 24th, our army had occupied Bailing Temple, which was a very important place for the bandits to entrenched themselves. When he heard my words at the time, a look of joy immediately appeared on his face; and he kept telling us about the customs and scenery of Suiyuan, and finally said: "The people of Suiyuan are very strong and not afraid of the cold. The weather there is so cold that the ears and noses will fall off." These words often made my colleagues listen with great interest.

Now we haven't seen him smoking for a long time, we asked him what the reason was? He replied to us like this:

"Sirs, you all take money to donate to fight the war, but I have no money and I can't be hungry every day and save the money for meals to help. So I have to quit smoking, and I have more than two yuan a month! And I decided to save it like this, and I must wait until these bandits and devils are wiped out and the war stops before stopping. After he finished speaking, a look of courage and hope appeared on his face, which really moved us. All the colleagues in the whole world, wake up, this is a critical moment of life and death!

The Phoenix Returns to Its Nest 181

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Nine, Making a Heartfelt Alliance over a Cup of Water, Speaking of Weariness under the Green Lamp, Making a Golden Promise, Reporting Yearning with Beans

Youmei smiled and said: So it seems that cousin also regards me as a literary confidante. As she spoke, she glanced at Guoqi, and immediately shook her hands together, smiling: I can't reach that high. Guoqi said: Once Miss Li becomes polite, she feels that everything is polite. Youmei smiled: This is not politeness. There is a saying that a real sword is given to a martyr, and beauty is given to a beauty. Giving something to someone means raising them up as something noble. Cousin gave me magazines, which means he often regards me as a lover of literature. Guoqi said: Can Miss Li still say that she is not a lover of literature? If you are not a lover of literature, you may not care about such idle matters as mine. Anyone who cares about this kind of thing has a bit of a bookish air. Youmei pursed her lips and smiled, twisted her body and said: I am a fool, a fool. But I am not qualified to add the word book. Guoqi has never had the courage to talk to women. Talking face-to-face with Youmei like this is partly because she is very forthright and does not have the shyness of a girl, and partly because they are relatives and have seen each other often. It was not difficult to say the serious entrustment or words of gratitude before, but now that they are gradually talking about jokes, he feels speechless again. So he also took a folding fan from the bookshelf and slowly fanned it in front of his chest. The room was extremely quiet, and the bamboo curtain hanging outside the window was shaking slightly, making a rustling sound. Youmei put her eyes on the books on the bookshelf, as if she was paying close attention to something, and then smiled: Cousin, most of the books on this bookshelf are about poetry. Guoqi said: It can't be said that there are many. I don't know that compared to the books on that bookshelf, there are a few more books about poetry. Youmei said: Cousin's poems are very well written. I will send a folding fan over and ask cousin to inscribe two lines of poetry on it, okay? Guoqi said: I can't write poetry... the next sentence of refusal. Before he could say it, Youmei turned her eyes and quickly shot him a glance. Guoqi had no choice but to hold back his words and immediately changed his tone and said: If Miss Li is not afraid that I will spoil the fan, then you can bring it. Youmei heard these words, as if she had obtained something desirable, narrowed her eyes and smiled on the bookshelf. Guoqi didn't know what her purpose was in coming here today. If it was to convey a message from Jiang Meng, this time it was completely irrelevant. (115)

Character Sketches

A Few Stories of "Paying Attention Only to Clothes" 182

— Geng Yuan

Mr. Zeng Zhaolun, who is now the head of the Department of Chemistry at Peking University, used to be the head of the Department of Chemistry at National Central University in Nanjing. Mr. Zeng has always been a practitioner of "native cloth doctrine" and looks like a country bumpkin. Once, National Central University held a school affairs meeting. The new president had just arrived and did not know Mr. Zeng. Coincidentally, only the new president and Mr. Zeng were on time for the meeting in the meeting room. After the president sat down, he thought that he was an impolite tea boy and ordered him to go out. Mr. Zeng calmly withdrew and said, "Since you invited me, you want me to leave again, that's really a joke." The president heard these words and knew that things were not good. After inquiring, he asked the tea boy to invite him again to attend the meeting. But this Zeng did not go, only instructed the tea boy to reply to the president: "I will wait until I go to Shanghai to change my clothes and then we will meet." The president was embarrassed and deeply ashamed of his negligence, so he entrusted many famous people to explain to Mr. Zeng again and again. Although no problem occurred later, it seemed that this president never got Mr. Zeng's understanding.

Mr. Weng Yongni, the current Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, is not only a geologist admired by the world, but also a consistent practitioner of frugality. When the Central Government intended to invite him to serve as Minister of Education but he declined last year, he went to Nanjing from Peiping and stayed at the Central Hotel. One day at noon, a certain minister invited him to dinner at his official residence. He wore a half-new, half-old silk robe, took a rickshaw, and went to the banquet calmly. How could he know that the doorman in the minister's official residence was used to seeing guests in cars and fancy clothes, plus there was no wealthy guest named Weng in their minds, so they kept him in the reception room for more than ten minutes, and said with a contemptuous tone: "Friend! Do you want to see the minister? There is something going on today, so I won't see guests. Come again in a few days." Mr. Weng thought that since everyone had something to do and could not keep the appointment, he had no choice but to go back. So he returned to the hotel without saying anything and asked the tea boy to prepare a meal for himself. Later, after one o'clock in the afternoon, the minister's phone call came to urge him, and he explained that he had invited the ministers to accompany him and had already arrived, etc. At this point, Mr. Weng suddenly understood, but he had no choice but to explain the situation. After hearing this, the minister was so embarrassed that he was speechless and had no choice but to apologize in person, but Mr. Weng never cared.

Director Cheng, who is in charge of a certain bureau in Shanghai, once wore a newly made cloth dress to a dinner party at the home of a certain famous person. After entering the door, he hesitated because he did not know the host. Coincidentally, a big man who looked like a cabinet member came to meet him. Without asking anything, he greeted him and said, "You are here." He followed him in and saw a small room with tea and cigarettes mixed together, and the layout was not bad. He casually ate something. Later, he felt that he had not seen the host and there were no acquaintances, so he greeted the people sitting with him, only to learn that these people were all followers and bodyguards of a certain member or a certain director. The director knew that he had misunderstood and had no choice but to leave quickly. Finally, he found the host and had dinner with the official guests.

Shenbao Local Supplement

Talks

Discussing the "Love Suicide" Incident of Students Studying in Japan 183

— Tian Yu

When it comes to the secrets between men and women, newspapers always have information worth exaggerating and vividly describing. Not to mention the so-called "love suicide," which is both tragic and intensely sensational?

Students studying in Japan, Zhu Zucai and Xue Yingzhi, attempted "love suicide" in Mihara, Japan, but failed. Two days later, the woman tried to commit suicide by taking poison in a Yokohama hotel. This kind of thing is actually quite common. However, it is said that Mihara has historically been a famous place for "love suicides" in Japan, and this is the first time Chinese people have patronized it. This is the first point worth exaggerating. Furthermore, the reason Zhu and Xue wanted to commit "love suicide" this time, besides the obvious reason of "love," is said to be because they were deeply saddened by the chaos in the country and the kidnapping of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. This reason is frighteningly noble. Who wouldn't respectfully stand at attention upon hearing of dying for the country? However, would "love suicide" by two people actually help rescue Chiang Kai-shek? Moreover, the reason of "love suicide" stemming from being saddened by national affairs is too difficult for people to understand. Chinese people like to put on airs. There's a joke: When the owner's wife of a tofu shop dies, the epitaph reads: "Awarded the title of Imperial Tutor and Grand Secretary of the Cabinet to the Honorable Consort's Next-Door Tofu Shop Owner's Wife, Madame XX." This is a satirical fable, and such a thing may not actually happen, but to attach the honorable term "dying for the country" to what is merely a love suicide is no different from the tofu shop owner's wife's epitaph usurping the title of the consort. I find it quite distasteful.

Even if it were truly for love, why resort to "love suicide"? The fulfillment of love is originally meant to bring joy to life, yet now people are choosing death for it. Some might say: this is Japanese culture. There are countless things we can learn from Japan, yet we insist on imitating this unproductive behavior. Is this really the purpose of studying in Japan? We truly feel heartbroken. Year after year, so-called overseas students go abroad, and over the decades, there must be hundreds of thousands of them. But to this day, we haven't seen many overseas students make any special contributions to China. On the contrary, those who can truly do something beneficial in China are not necessarily overseas-educated students. Of course, we cannot deny that there are some outstanding talents among overseas students, but their number is too small. It seems that they have let themselves and the country down.

A friend who recently returned from Japan said that in Tokyo's nightlife, including dance halls and tea houses, two-thirds of the long-term customers are Chinese students. This is probably true. He also said that our friendly nation provides special protection for Chinese students, especially cherishing the sons and daughters who are wealthy and can spend lavishly. It is said that if a problem were to occur between China and Japan and all the students studying in Japan returned home, half of the dance halls and tea houses in Tokyo alone would have to close down. This is such a heartbreaking fact. Although this has no direct relationship with Zhu and Xue's love suicide, it is still worth mentioning.

A muddled life, it seems, can no longer last. One day, a day of flying blood and flesh will come, and it will be judged who can truly stand tall and walk the path of survival, and who will fall into the eighteenth level of hell!

Taoran Pavilion 184

— You Qi

It is quite strange. My residence, which has always been little noticed, has somehow taken a turn. Now, it is not only a topic of casual conversation for people in my hometown after tea and wine, but also evokes dreams and aspirations in the South, the mountain cities, and any place where culture reaches.

Isn't that so? When people travel to Beiping and get off the train, if you ask what good places there are to visit, the answer is almost always the same: the Summer Palace and the Longevity Hill if you go a little further, or Beihai, Zhongnanhai, and Zhongshan Park if you stay closer. If you have a sense of history, they will tell you where Tiananmen is and where Jingshan is, so that travelers can appreciate the magnificent and beautiful scenery, the lush waters and verdant mountains, the residence of the imperial family, which is so enviable!

But the Taoran Pavilion, right near me, is easily placed at the back of their minds. Putting it at the back of their minds is understandable. Reeds and graveyards surround the entire solitary pavilion. If you shout, you will hear only a faint echo, and you will hear no human voice. It quietly allows the years to slip by. Moreover, the "Nanxia Wazi" nearby – the slum – is viewed no differently than the people of Shanghai view the Jiangbei grass shacks. It is messy, filthy, and moldy. In short, it is not a place for high-class people to "glance" at, so why give visitors a bad impression?

Perhaps it's just that I was born lowly. From my youth to my childhood, I liked the Nanxia Wazi that people looked down on, and I also liked the quiet and lonely Taoran Pavilion.

In spring, the warmth in the North comes relatively late. During the Qingming Festival, the grass grows and the swallows fly. From my residence at the head of "Nanheng Street," I would turn with two or three companions of similar age and walk onto "Heiyaochang." This street is not long. At its southern end is the "Sansheng Temple," where Sai Jinhua, who once shone brightly in our lives, once stayed. The temple is quite large and elegantly decorated. Further south, the Nanxia Wazi comes into view. The so-called "Wazi" was originally just a lower-lying area with ponds and marshes and few residents. Gradually, those whose livelihoods did not allow them to live within the Forbidden City sought ways to move here. Thus, this place was developed into a special environment. Further down, you pass through a stately pavilion with large doorways at the bottom and a small Buddha enshrined in a small room on the upper floor. The "Yaotai" is like a dirt mountain, dilapidated beyond recognition, standing in front of the pavilion's door. Walking up, you see that several broken temples have damaged walls. In one corner, two leaning shacks have been built, inhabited by two elderly couples. If a strong wind were to come, it could either bury them in the rubble or blow them down along with their houses. In the past, this was a "kiln," with a raging fire burning, sending batches of goods to "Heiyaochang." But the historical sites? They have vanished like passing clouds, leaving only memories of the past! A few years ago, it was said that there were still traces of the filled-in kiln openings, but now they are covered by weeds.

Following the flat road, you pass by reed ponds on both sides. The warm spring breeze ripples through the wilderness, and the sun melts the thick layer of ice. The wrinkles ripple in the direction of the wind, shimmering. The deep-rooted reed seedlings sprout vigorously. Ah, here lies buried our beloved childhood, and it also contains countless historical sites worth reminiscing about—

At the end of the road is Taoran Pavilion. The two gates are always closed. In spring, when the chilly winds have not yet subsided, there are few visitors. When summer comes, unable to bear the heat, people wave their banana leaf fans and stroll in the serene surroundings, one after another, as the sun falls behind Fragrant Hills. If you want to stay longer and sit comfortably for a while, you can go to the pavilion. There is tea and hot towels, and the cost is limited. Standing under the veranda-like corridor and looking south, you see the outer city wall not far away, black and jagged, extending to the city gate tower and then stretching to the distant horizon. The other three sides are reed ponds, with reeds taller than people. Wild birds (bird name) hide here, chirping noisily. The moonlight engulfs the entire wilderness. Take in the magnificent sound of the clams, the surroundings are silent, and a gentle breeze passes by your ear. You can't help but feel a sense of tranquility.

In autumn, the tips of the reeds are covered in grayish-white ears, and the fluff floats, floats. The crickets raise their voices in loud cries. The reed branches rustle, slender and desolate. Slowly, the severe frost erodes their existence, and the pond turns yellow again. Where are the people of Taoran? They have long since stepped onto the heated kang to warm themselves. What remains is the lonely and desolate Taoran Pavilion!

It has been several years since I left that despised place. I never imagined that it would be mentioned again because of a "beauty of a generation." In this harsh winter, I think Taoran Pavilion will not break the dull atmosphere because of the beauty's fragrant tomb, right?

Bridge 185

— Shen Bing

A bridge is like a stupid person with a hunched back, lying on a flat road, obstructing people, animals, and the winter scenery.

The bridge saves the cooking smoke of broken boats entering the home, but even the rusty tin chimneys cannot reach the bridge and pass under the bridge arch. Look at the broken reed mat hanging on the cabin, fanned by the wind. It's cold. What gives people a sense of warmth is a clay stove for roasting sweet potatoes at the end of the bridge.

The old woman selling roasted sweet potatoes is dressed like children, her cotton-padded jacket is bloated, her shoes are bloated, and her neck is bloated. The children have red cheeks and snot hanging from their noses. They hide under the wall, watching the old woman selling roasted sweet potatoes with greedy eyes.

The northwest wind, carrying ice and snow, grabs the chest of the wall, making a sad hissing sound. The room with the stove is warm, but the children only have frozen black hands and a basket, which will hold the jade scavenged from the garbage mountain.

The old woman selling roasted sweet potatoes stretches out a hand as withered as life itself, picks up the iron tongs, and pulls a well-roasted sweet potato from the stove. A smell of burnt sweet potato emerges from the stove, scattering in the strong and piercing wind.

The children drag their clothes and wipe away the watery snot.

The garbage truck with iron wheels is coming again. The cart puller bends over and climbs over from the other end of the bridge. The children run over in a puff of smoke, helping the old cart puller push the cart to the garbage mountain as if they were welcoming their father.

Greedy black hands grab and sweep on the garbage heap, but it's cold.

The garbage truck is pulled onto the bridge again, and the bridge makes a creaking groan. The bridge is like a stupid person with a hunched back, lying on a flat road, obstructing people, animals, and the winter scenery.

Old Friend 186

— Lin Ji

Whenever I am free and have nothing to do, I have a habit that has not changed for several years: I like to take a book or a few newspapers to a tea house and sit there for an hour or two, read the newspapers, drink a cup of light Longjing tea, watch the people coming and going in the tea house, and savor the happiness of leisure.

Through the glass window, it is gradually getting dark on a cold winter night. The wind must be blowing hard, every pedestrian shrinks their forehead into the collar of their upturned coat, white air coming out of their mouths. The trams are full of people returning home, rumbling past. Hiding myself inside the window and watching the activities of people on the street is a different kind of feeling.

Because it's already past tea time, there are only a few scattered people left here. One table is eating their dinner. Right next to that table full of sugar-fried spare ribs, braised fish head, and oily chicken, I found a face that was extremely familiar, but I couldn't remember his name for a moment. His head was originally lowered, but then he suddenly straightened up and noticed me. The pointed chin, the long face, the prominent nose, only his hair was longer, wasn't this – we both stood up, I walked faster and ran to his opposite, asking him:

"Are you He Zhicheng, a graduate of Provincial Fifth Middle School?"

"Yes," he stretched out his hand and shook mine; I immediately felt that his hand was very thin and cold, and he quickly retracted it. He still remembered me, said my name, and continued, "You're still so young, you haven't changed at all! We, we haven't seen each other for five years, right?"

I nodded and sat down. I may not have changed much, but he has really changed too much. From the lines on his forehead, you could tell how much of the world's hardships he had gone through in the past few years. We lived in the same dormitory when we were in middle school; whenever the night was quiet, we were reluctant to go to sleep and liked to talk about our hopes and grand ambitions. I remember him saying to me: "My most pressing hope right now is to be able to go to Shanghai to study at a university next year, as I wish. Although the environment we are in now is not good, and the current society is dark, we young people must rise up and transform it!" The following year, he did get the opportunity to go to university in the midst of his poverty. We came to Shanghai on the same boat. But after the exam, we were admitted to different schools, so our years of studying together were suddenly separated! At that time, we still met often, still maintaining our youthful innocence, always talking about our ambition to transform society. When we were in our third year of university, the unfortunate news came that his father had passed away in a painful illness, without having the time to see his son succeed! And the burden of the family's livelihood immediately shifted to the shoulders of this 23-year-old youth. At that time, I was traveling in Nanjing, and when I returned to Shanghai, I only received a short letter from him saying that he had decided to go home, but his whereabouts after that were still uncertain... And from then on, he never gave me any news, which made me feel very strange. Now, we have unexpectedly reunited, and he explained to me that people struggling in the torrent of life sometimes really have no opportunity to write letters. I myself am currently in this state, so I understand him very well. He told me that in the past five years, he had been running around, and in order to make a living, he had even been a soldier. The more he talked about his difficult life experiences, the more moved I became.

"Coming to Shanghai, because I didn't know if you were still here – even if you were, I couldn't find out your address, so if we didn't run into each other in the tea house, I'm afraid I wouldn't know when we would meet!" he ended like this.

So, I told him my address and briefly told him about my own life situation.

"It's really getting worse day by day!" We both lamented together.

It was already dark outside, and the city's night was noisy. I saw that it was getting late, and I had to attend a friend's meeting that night, so I said goodbye to him and came out. The cold wind was blowing hard outside, sparse stars were twinkling in the sky, and the big clock on top of a Western-style building was striking nine o'clock – dong, dong, dong... the sound struck my heart with unusual heaviness.

Cao Xiaoying "Jade Dragonfly"

Central and Western (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening Chapter "Tears and Laughter, the Story of Love"

The general glares angrily, eyes wide, wielding a rattan whip, ascending the stairs. Unprepared. I went to Tianjin yesterday because of something. And you, secretly slipped out. Alas, you lowly person. One lash. One curse. The hand waves and the eyes follow, without stopping. But see, snow-white skin and cloud-like hair disheveled. Clothing disheveled, revealing the chest. Fengxi listens. Trembling. Perspiration dripping from head to toe. Ears on the wall will eventually detect. How can there be no eavesdroppers outside the window. Who would have thought, the general, in a fit of rage, heard these words. Suddenly, he sneered a few times. I know everything in your heart. Could it be, a secret rendezvous renewing old feelings. I thought, you were a humble resident of a poor lane. Making a living by singing and playing clappers. Now you haven't changed your usual ways. I'm afraid, your foxy tail will show. I thought you had changed your tune and dressed as a scholar. Transforming into a respectable female student. Coming here, to enjoy wealth and luxury. Dressed in silk and eating delicacies, pleasing your heart. Who knew, your bones were naturally seductive. You couldn't hide the fleeting affair. You actually, secretly put a cuckold's hat on me. Grass and wormwood are not noble. They are like roadside willows, wall flowers, and wild grasses. How can a swallow produce a phoenix? Of course, you are not destined to be a lady.

Jiang Binchu "Three Smiles"

New Sound (1380) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening Chapter "Roar! China" (Written by Chen Shaomin) The beautiful land of China for five thousand years. Founding the nation, dominating East Asia, at the center. Today, the countryside is bankrupt, the city is emaciated. Internal and external troubles are pressing in. Under iron hooves, the strong enemy arbitrarily destroys our land. Overwhelming oppression is truly unbearable. Might even extinguishes justice. The beautiful divine land has come to this. How many are the brave children of China? Aspiring to save the nation today. Urgent. Difficult. Unrepentant in dedicating oneself to the country. Smiling as you go to the battlefield. For justice. For peace. A hundred battles, a hundred victories, establish the great. We would rather break our heads. Than change our will. Not killing the enemy. Swear not to return. Willing to donate our heads for the nation. Not afraid of the enemy's guns and cannons. From now on, emulate the former sages and sleep on firewood and taste gall. Long-term resistance requires unity. Do not be indecisive and fickle. How can you love yourself when your country is destroyed? Jade and stone burned together is truly unbearable. I urge you all, love your family, first love your country. Preserving every inch of land is the top priority. Living in peace and working happily is what everyone desires. When that time comes, the world will be for the public to freely discuss. World peace and national prosperity will come.
